### Snackbar

> Snackbars inform users of a process that an app has performed or will perform. They appear temporarily, towards the bottom of the screen. They shouldn’t interrupt the user experience, and they don’t require user input to disappear. Accepts `Supporting text#53937:0`, `Configuration`, `# of lines`, `Show close affordance` properties.

**Properties:**

- `Configuration`: `Text only` | `Text & action` | `Text & longer action` (default: `Text only`)
- `# of lines`: `One line` | `Two lines` (default: `One line`)
- `Show close affordance`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)

### Slider

> Sliders allow users to view and select a value (or range) along a track. They’re ideal for adjusting settings such as volume and brightness, or for applying image filters.

Choose from 0%, 25%, 50% 75% and 100% variants Accepts `Type`, `State`, `Percentage` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Type`: `Continuous` | `Discrete` (default: `Continuous`)
- `State`: `Enabled` | `Hovered` | `Focused` | `Pressed` | `Disabled` (default: `Enabled`)

### Linear progress indicator

> Progress indicators inform users about the status of ongoing processes, such  as loading an app, submitting a form, or saving updates. They communicate an app’s state and indicate available actions, such as whether users can navigate away from  the current screen.

Choose between 25%, 50%, 75% 100% variants or customize your own using the right padding value. Accepts `Progress` property.

**Properties:**
- `Progress`: `100%` | `25%` | `50%` | `75%` | `Custom (advanced)` (default: `25%`)

---

### Navigation Rail

> The rail is a side navigation component that displays three to seven app destinations and, optionally, a floating action button (FAB). Each destination is represented by an icon and label text.

The rail can serve as the sole navigation component on larger screen sizes, such as desktops and tablets.

🛠 Additional options
Segments - Can be edited by selecting individual segments and  selecting states, labels, and badges from the variant properties. Accepts `FAB#52510:0`, `Alignment` properties.

**Properties:**
- `FAB#52510:0`: boolean (default: `true`)
- `Alignment`: `Bottom` | `Middle` | `Top` (default: `Top`)

### Navigation Drawer

> Navigation drawers provide access to destinations and app functionality, such as switching accounts. They can either be permanently on-screen or opened and closed by a navigation menu icon.

Navigation drawers are recommended for apps with 5 or more top-level destinations, apps with 2 or more levels of navigation hierarchy, quick navigation between unrelated destinations, or replacing the navigation rail or navigation bar on large screens.

🛠 Additional options 
Nav Item - Can be edited by selecting individual item and  selecting style, states, icons, and metadata from the variant properties.

### Navigation bar

> Navigation bars (nav bars) provide access to three to five destinations.

The nav bar is positioned at the bottom of screens for convenient access. Each destination is represented by an icon and optional text label.
When a navigation bar icon is tapped or focused, the user is taken to the navigation destination associated with that icon. 

Use on mobile or tablet only.

🛠 Additional options 
Segments - can be edited by selecting individual segments and  selecting states, labels, and badges from the variant properties. Accepts `Configuration`, `Segments` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Configuration`: `icon & label` | `icon` (default: `icon & label`)
- `Segments`: `3` | `4` | `5` (default: `3`)

---

### Icon button

> Icon buttons display actions in a compact layout. Icon buttons can represent opening actions such as opening an overflow menu or search, or represent binary actions that can be toggled on and off, such as favorite or bookmark.

Icon buttons can be grouped together or they can stand alone. Accepts `Icon#52081:6`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52081:6`: component instance
- `Style`: `filled` | `outlined` | `standard` | `tonal` (default: `standard`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `disabled` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Icon button toggleable

> Icon buttons display actions in a compact layout. Icon buttons can represent opening actions such as opening an overflow menu or search, or represent binary actions that can be toggled on and off, such as favorite or bookmark.

Icon buttons can be grouped together or they can stand alone. Accepts `Icon (selected)#52081:48`, `Icon (unselected)#52081:89`, `Style`, `State`, `Selected` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon (selected)#52081:48`: component instance
- `Icon (unselected)#52081:89`: component instance
- `Style`: `filled` | `outlined` | `standard` | `tonal` (default: `standard`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `disabled` (default: `enabled`)
- `Selected`: `false` | `true` (default: `false`)

---

### Small FAB

> Use Floating action buttons (FABs) for the most important action (primary action) on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center.

A small FAB is used for a secondary, supporting action, or in place of a default FAB on smaller screens. Accepts `Icon#52946:0`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:0`: component instance
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### FAB

> Floating action buttons (FABs) help people take primary actions on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center. Accepts `Icon#52946:34`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:34`: component instance
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Large FAB

> Floating action buttons (FABs) help people take primary actions on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center.

A large FAB is useful when the layout calls for a clear and prominent primary action, and where a larger footprint would help the user engage. Accepts `Icon#52946:68`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:68`: component instance
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Extended FAB

> Extended FABs are used on screens with long, scrolling views that require persistent access to an action, such as a check-out screen. Do not use an extended FAB in a view that cannot scroll.

The FAB can transform into an extended FAB if the screen size is increased, such as when a mobile view is expanded into a desktop view. Accepts `Icon#52946:102`, `Label text#53923:602`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:102`: component instance
- `Label text#53923:602`: text
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Small FAB-dark

> Use Floating action buttons (FABs) for the most important action (primary action) on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center.

A small FAB is used for a secondary, supporting action, or in place of a default FAB on smaller screens. Accepts `Icon#52946:17`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:17`: component instance
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### FAB-dark

> Floating action buttons (FABs) help people take primary actions on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center. Accepts `Icon#52946:51`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52946:51`: component instance
- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Large FAB-dark

> Floating action buttons (FABs) help people take primary actions on a screen. The FAB appears in front of all other content on screen, and is recognizable for its rounded shape and icon in the center.

A large FAB is useful when the layout calls for a clear and prominent primary action, and where a larger footprint would help the user engage. Accepts `Icon#52946:85`, `Style`, `State` properties.

**Properties:**

- `Style`: `surface` | `primary` | `secondary` | `tertiary` (default: `surface`)

### Basic dialog

> A Dialog is a modal window that appears in front of app content to provide critical information or ask for a decision. They disable all app functionality when they appear, and remain on screen until a required action has been taken.

Being purposefully interruptive they should be used sparingly. To provide options without interrupting a user’s experience use a Menu. Accepts `Divider#52161:0`, `Icon` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Divider#52161:0`: boolean (default: `false`)
- `Icon`: `true` | `false` (default: `false`)

---

### List dialog

> A Dialog is a modal window that appears in front of app content to provide critical information or ask for a decision. They disable all app functionality when they appear, and remain on screen until a required action has been taken.

Being purposefully interruptive they should be used sparingly. To provide options without interrupting a user’s experience use a Menu.

🛠 Additional options 
List item - can be edited by selecting an individual list item and  selecting states, leading icons, trailing icons, and dividers from the variant properties. Accepts `Icon` property.

**Properties:**
- `Icon`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)

---

### Scrollable list dialog

> A Dialog is a modal window that appears in front of app content to provide critical information or ask for a decision. They disable all app functionality when they appear, and remain on screen until a required action has been taken.

Most dialog content should avoid scrolling. Even when scrolling is required, the dialog title is pinned at the top, with buttons pinned at the bottom. Dialogs don’t scroll with elements outside of the dialog, such as the background.

Being purposefully interruptive they should be used sparingly. To provide options without interrupting a user’s experience use a Menu.

🛠 Additional options 
List item - can be edited by selecting an individual list item and  selecting states, leading icons, trailing icons, and dividers from the variant properties. Accepts `Icon` property.

**Properties:**
- `Icon`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)

---

### Input chip

> Input chips represent discrete pieces of information entered by a user, such as Gmail contacts or filter options within a search field. Accepts `Leading icon#52999:63`, `Avatar#52999:112`, `Label text#53923:102`, `Configuration`, `State`, `Selected`, `Show closing icon` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Leading icon#52999:63`: component instance
- `Avatar#52999:112`: component instance
- `Label text#53923:102`: text
- `Configuration`: `label only` | `label & leading icon` | `label & avatar` (default: `label only`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `dragged` (default: `enabled`)
- `Selected`: `false` | `true` (default: `false`)
- `Show closing icon`: `false` | `true` (default: `false`)

---

### Assistive chip

> Assist chips represent smart or automated actions that can span multiple apps. They should appear dynamically and contextually in a UI. Accepts `Leading icon#52999:308`, `Branded icon#52999:357`, `Favicon#52999:406`, `Label text#53923:151`, `Style`, `Configuration`, `State` properties.

- `Configuration`: `label only` | `label & icon` | `label & favicon` | `label & brand icon` (default: `label only`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `dragged` | `disabled` (default: `enabled`)

---

### Filter chip

> Filter chips use tags or descriptive words to filter content. They can be a good alternative to toggle buttons or checkboxes.

Tapping on a filter chip activates it and appends a leading checkmark icon to the starting edge of the chip label. Accepts `Trailing icon#52999:602`, `Leading icon#52999:699`, `Label text#53923:200`, `Style`, `Configuration`, `State`, `Selected`, `Show trailing icon` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Trailing icon#52999:602`: component instance
- `Leading icon#52999:699`: component instance
- `Label text#53923:200`: text
- `Style`: `outlined` | `elevated` (default: `outlined`)
- `Configuration`: `label only` | `label & leading icon` (default: `label only`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `dragged` | `disabled` (default: `enabled`)
- `Selected`: `false` | `true` (default: `false`)
- `Show trailing icon`: `false` | `true` (default: `false`)

---

### Carousel

> A Carousel contains a collection of items that can be scrolled on and off the screen.

🛠️
Select between Uniform and Non-uniform layouts;
Choose Mobile or Tablet context
An optional item-text’s visibility can be toggled on and off Accepts `Text content#59:0`, `Uniform`, `Context` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Text content#59:0`: boolean (default: `false`)
- `Uniform`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)
- `Context`: `Mobile` | `Tablet` (default: `Mobile`)

---

###  Carousel-item-text
_Path: Building Blocks/ Carousel-item-text_

> Carousel items are primarily visual. Item text is optional and should be brief. If your carousel items require a lot of text, consider using a series of cards instead. Text should always be understandable at each size. Consider adapting the text to use brief labels on smaller carousel items.

🛠️
Supporting text visibility can be turned on and off in the properties panel Accepts `Supporting Text` property.

**Properties:**
- `Supporting Text`: `True` | `False` (default: `False`)

---

### Horizontal card-dark

> Cards are used to display content and actions on a single topic. They should be easy to scan for relevant and actionable information. Cards can be displayed together in a grid, vertical list, or carousel. Accepts `Style` property.

**Properties:**
- `Style`: `Outlined` | `Elevated` | `Filled` (default: `Outlined`)

---

> Outlined component. Accepts `state` property.

- `state`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `dragged` (default: `enabled`)

### Button

> Buttons communicate actions that users can take. They are typically placed throughout your UI, in places like Dialogs, Modal windows, Forms, Cards and Toolbars Accepts `Icon#52590:56`, `Label text#53923:0`, `Style`, `State`, `Show Icon` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Icon#52590:56`: component instance
- `Label text#53923:0`: text
- `Style`: `Filled` | `Outlined` | `Text` | `Elevated` | `Tonal` (default: `Filled`)
- `State`: `enabled` | `hovered` | `focused` | `pressed` | `disabled` (default: `enabled`)
- `Show Icon`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)

---

### Bottom sheet

> Bottom sheets are surfaces containing supplementary content,  anchored to the bottom of the screen.

🛠 Additional options 
Drag handle - can be toggled to hide or show Accepts `Show Drag handle#52079:0`, `Modal` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Show Drag handle#52079:0`: boolean (default: `true`)
- `Modal`: `False` | `True` (default: `False`)

### Bottom app bar

> "Bottom app bars provide access to up to four actions, including the floating action button (FAB). Bottom app bars should be used for mobile devices only

🛠  Additional options 
Icon buttons - Change Icon buttons by selecting the individual icon buttons and editing the variant properties for states and icon values.

FAB - Change the FAB by selecting the FAB and editing the variant properties for states." Accepts `Show FAB#52994:0`, `Icons` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Show FAB#52994:0`: boolean (default: `true`)
- `Icons`: `1` | `2` | `3` | `4` (default: `1`)

---

### Bottom app bar-dark

FAB - Change the FAB by selecting the FAB and editing the variant properties for states." Accepts `Show FAB#52994:9`, `Icons` properties.

**Properties:**

### Badge

> Badges are used to indicate a notification, item count, or other information relating to a navigation destination. They are placed on the ending edge of icons, typically within other components. Accepts `Badge label (single digit)#52867:8`, `Badge label (multiple digits)#52867:20`, `Size` properties.

**Properties:**
- `Badge label (single digit)#52867:8`: text
- `Badge label (multiple digits)#52867:20`: text
- `Size`: `Small` | `Large-Single Digit` | `Multiple Digits` (default: `Small`)

---

## Design Constraints

- **Primary font**: Figtree

> Do not use raw hex values or hardcoded sizes — always reference tokens by name.
